  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1149889255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149889255" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149889255?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679412731" href="/book/show/415961.Fatherland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=alternative-history">alternative-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149889255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4426609889398822026">Fatherland takes a well worn subject, what if Nazi Germany had been successful in WWII, and takes an unusual avenue to explore it. Unlike other books on the subject Fatherland does not concern itself with the big military picture and it doesn't dally in the political decisions that changed history. It takes the changes as a given and explores this strange and horrifying world through the eyes of a simple police officer trying to solve a crime. It infuses a 1960's Nazi dominated Europe with all t</span>
  <span id="freeText4426609889398822026" style="display:none">Fatherland takes a well worn subject, what if Nazi Germany had been successful in WWII, and takes an unusual avenue to explore it. Unlike other books on the subject Fatherland does not concern itself with the big military picture and it doesn't dally in the political decisions that changed history. It takes the changes as a given and explores this strange and horrifying world through the eyes of a simple police officer trying to solve a crime. It infuses a 1960's Nazi dominated Europe with all the recognizable elements of a noir mystery thriller: abuse of power, a femme fatale, a man just trying to find truth in an otherwise corrupt system, death, deception, and double crosses.<br /><br />The world that this story takes place in is indeed a depressing one. Nazi Germany has come to dominate Europe and is locked into a cold war with the United States. Xavier March, a member of the German police, is called out to a strange crime scene that propels him down the rabbit hole of Nazi secrets, power plays, and lost history. All the keystones of classic Noir setting are present in this book, but with much higher stakes because, you know, Nazis.<br /><br />Harris does a top notch job introducing the reader to this strange world. Tantalizing hints are dropped about how this world in different but it never becomes the focus of the book. He explores just what it would be like to live under a Nazi police state through the eyes of a war Veteran that remembers life before the party and is somewhat disenchanted with its ideology. We see how such a society warps and controls children, replacing family, community, or religion with the Party and the State as a center for loyalty. It creates a nation of followers that Harris brilliantly portrays and March cunningly exploits at various points in the book.<br /><br />Because of this setting the acceptable bounds of behavior of the bad guys is much wider. That cop who threatens to put a bullet in your head isn't crooked, he is just following orders from higher up and would likely get a commendation for his act. March himself is a part of the system and faces the unique challenge of seeking the truth in an environment that is both hostile and fatal for the seekers of certain truths.<br /><br />Harris also sets up the politics of Nazi Germany quite well. It isn't some monolithic entity of pure evil, but a highly bureaucratic one with many factions vying for power. Harris explores the dark nooks and crannies of the Nazi power structure through March's investigation and gives the reader a good feel for what the banality of evil looks like writ large (spoiler alert: it doesn't look good).<br /><br />What I most enjoyed about this book was how vibrant the characters were. Relationships felt natural and organic. The repartee with March and his partner (see below) were great and felt like a friendship that was many years old. The SS officers' behaviors made sense within the context of their character and you even feel a bit a sympathy for one towards the end. While I typically get very little out of romantic plot lines, the American reporter that March falls in with was also a great, fully realized character instead of just being a pretty face and love interest.<br /><br />Finally, the prose in this book was outstanding. Harris really knows how to effectively turn a phrase using the voice of his characters:<br /><br /><i>"That was how it was with young men of his age. They had come off an assembly line of Pimpf, Hitler Youth, National Service and Strength-through-Joy. They heard the same speeches, read the same slogans, eaten the same one pot meals in aid of Winter Relief. They were the regime's workhorses, had known no authority but the party, and we're as reliable as the Kripo's Volkswagens."</i><br /><br />~~~<br /><br /><i>"What do you do if you devote your life to discovering criminals, and it gradually occurs to you that the real criminals are the people you work for?"<br />"I suppose you go crazy."<br />"Or worse. Sane."</i><br /><br />~~~<br /><br /><i>"If you think Fuhrertag </i>[Hitler's Birthday]<i> is a security nightmare - forget it. Can you imagine what it'll be like with Kennedy in town as well?"<br />"I think, Max, you are missing the historic dimension of the occasion."<br />"Screw the historic dimension of the occasion. I'm thinking about my sleep..."</i><br /><br />~~~<br /><br /><i>"...What did you expect to pick up at the morgue?"<br />"Plenty."<br />"What? Be exact!"<br />Fleas. Lice. A skin rash from his shitty clothes."</i><br /><br />Sharp, insightful, witty, all hallmarks of a writing style I greatly enjoy.<br /><br />All in all this was a great book that I enjoyed reading a lot. Some of that may be due to my love of WWII history (of which this book does delve in to), but I found the setting engrossing, the characters engaging, and the plot both surprising and perfectly reasonable. It kept me guessing what would happen next and followed its internal consistency its natural end. While I doubt he will, I would love it if Harris would write another book or twenty set in this alternate world.<br /><br />Fatherland is definitely worth checking out for those who enjoy alternative histories, WWII, thrillers, or some combination of the three.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4426609889398822026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1149889255">

<div id="review_1243645682" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243645682" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41609617-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539156508p2/41609617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243645682?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/41609617-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/17313706-fatherland">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243645682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16712733947984412404">Robert Harris' brilliantly thrilling and thought-provoking debut novel - set in a post WWII (1960's) alternative Germany; one where Nazi Germany had previously won the war. An excellent thriller set against a wonderfully imagined and evoked backdrop of a world that so very easily might have been... <br/><br/>The first of many excellent thrillers from the pen of Robert Harris, but this is where it all started.<br/><br/>Not to be missed.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1802688848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802688848" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12798350-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564684546p2/12798350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802688848?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/12798350-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812977219" href="/book/show/396250.Fatherland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12798350-andrew?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12798350-andrew?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802688848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4245876852518344110">Fatherland by Robert Harris, is a book of alternate history set in 1964 Germany. This is a Germany where the Nazi's won WWII, took large swathes of territory, reorganized Europe in their own image, and continue to fight Russian partisans in the Ural mountains. The book follows a German Kripo, Xavier March, who is called to inspect a dead body in a river in Berlin. The body is of one Josef Buhler, who was a member an administrator in the General Government region in WWII. Buhler is a top Nazi pol</span>
  <span id="freeText4245876852518344110" style="display:none">Fatherland by Robert Harris, is a book of alternate history set in 1964 Germany. This is a Germany where the Nazi's won WWII, took large swathes of territory, reorganized Europe in their own image, and continue to fight Russian partisans in the Ural mountains. The book follows a German Kripo, Xavier March, who is called to inspect a dead body in a river in Berlin. The body is of one Josef Buhler, who was a member an administrator in the General Government region in WWII. Buhler is a top Nazi politician, and the investigation begins to arouse the attention of the Gestapo. March, in typical hard-bitten detective fashion, cannot let this one go. He begins to suspect something greater is at stake, as Germany and the USA begin a Detente to end their "cold war" and the Gestapo begin to take a greater interest in the case. Soon, March is on the run with a beautiful American reporter as the conspiracy ramps up, and unsettling questions about Nazi Germany's past begin to come to the surface.<br /><br />Potential Spoilers from here on: <i> you've been warned!</i><br /><br />Robert Harris has written a fascinating book about an alternate history where Germany has won WWII, by tying in a small time detective and a murder case out of his league. Germany is a police state in 1964: travel permits are given out only with strict permission, everyone is a Gestapo informant, and the state is run both in the image of an ageing Hitler and as a total police state, not unlike East Germany at this time in actual history. <br /><br />The story unravels slowly. March begins to have suspicions that the Gestapo are involved, and finds ties to other dead Party members over the past decade. He uses his contacts and friends, as well as those of his American friend Charlotte. However, it is difficult to know who to trust. Informants are everywhere. The Americans and Germans are working toward Detente, and do not want things to go awry. Joseph Kennedy is looking to be elected again for a third term in office in the US, and the Detente would go along way to improving his ratings at home. <br /><br />It begins to pick up as March gets deeper into the case, and begins to question the facts surrounding it and how much the Gestapo already know. Three of the dead party leaders, including Buhler, were part of an art ring with spoils from wartime Poland, leading him to a secret account in a Zurich bank. The men were also invited to a mysterious meeting in 1942 by Heydrich to discuss an important matter, but all records have vanished. Something bigger begins to emerge than just the murder. A horrifying secret is buried, and March sets out to find what it is.<br /><br />Harris' book is an excellent work of fiction, but ties in historical detail. Many of the Nazi and American politicians in the book are real. Reinhard Heydrich was one of the architects of the holocaust, who in reality was assassinated in 1942. Buhler, and other murdered Nazi's, including Martin Luther and others, were actually present at a meeting in 1942 to plan and implement the holocaust. Nebe, Xavier March's boss, was part of the holocaust in Belarus as a member of the SS unit who rounded up and murdered Jews behind the front lines. He was later implemented in a plot to assassinate Hitler, but in this timeline became Chief of the Kripo and is a rival of Heydrich's. Harris uses real transcripts and meeting minutes as evidence in this book. He also uses minutes of Joseph Kennedy, who notoriously made anti-Semitic comments during a diplomatic meeting in Germany in 1938.<br /><br />A lot of thought went into this mystery book. The feeling of the mystery of the Holocaust coming to light is fascinating. Germany did try to cover their death camps during WWII, and if they had won, it is likely that few questions would have been asked about them. Harris also turns history on its head. The world decries the Soviets instead, and their Gulag system and political massacres are abhorred in a similar way to Nazi crimes today. The use of real life Nazi's and what happened to them after the war is also fascinating. This is a wonderful alternate history novel with touches of Neo-Noir fiction, hard bitten detective, and dystopic fiction, as well as the alternate history of course, this book is a really interesting read, and not to be missed if you are into these sorts of genres. Recommended for history/alt-history buffs, and those who like a good detective story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4245876852518344110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_417838381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417838381" />
    <a title="Dyuti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5486168-dyuti"><img alt="Dyuti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351864861p2/5486168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417838381?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dyuti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dyuti" href="/user/show/5486168-dyuti">Dyuti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5486168-dyuti?shelf=holocast-or-ww2">holocast-or-ww2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5486168-dyuti?shelf=crime-thriller-mystery">crime-thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417838381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6928964761840674700">I chanced upon this book after reading Stephen's wonderful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115504120' rel='nofollow noopener'> review</a> while here on Goodreads. <br/><br/>Indeed, the blurb got me so hooked, that for the next four months I tried to hunt it down. But after futile visits to ALL the city bookstores with my boyfriend, who is also an avid reader, I finally gave up! Apparently, it was out of circulation. And right when I thought I would never be able lay my hands on it, I found a copy on sale on the Internet. A brand new 20th anniversary edition that too. So, I s</span>
  <span id="freeText6928964761840674700" style="display:none">I chanced upon this book after reading Stephen's wonderful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115504120" rel="nofollow noopener"> review</a> while here on Goodreads. <br /><br />Indeed, the blurb got me so hooked, that for the next four months I tried to hunt it down. But after futile visits to ALL the city bookstores with my boyfriend, who is also an avid reader, I finally gave up! Apparently, it was out of circulation. And right when I thought I would never be able lay my hands on it, I found a copy on sale on the Internet. A brand new 20th anniversary edition that too. So, I seized my chance. <br /><br /><i>I was not disappointed.</i><br /><br /><b>Plot:</b><br /><br />In his debut novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/575.Robert_Harris" title="Robert Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Harris</a> writes an alternate history of what <i>would have happened</i> had Germany defeated the Allies in the 2nd World War. It is set in 1964, in the week preceding the Feuher's 75th Birthday. A body floats up in the Havel, and a middle aged SS officer starts investigating the case. Soon he starts digging out secrets and lies long buried, which makes him a target for those who don't want his interference. <br /><br />As Harris puts it<i>"I like the conceit of having an honest policeman working for a criminal regime; a detective investigating a single death in a society founded on the greatest act of mass murder in history."</i><br /><br />However there were a few things which I <b>disliked</b> too...<br /><br />1. The romance which the author developed between the protagonists seemed a bit contrived. I mean, it did not seem natural. It's absence would not have made difference to the story in any way. <br /><br />2. The ending did not seem very well rounded. I do not mean that it was abrupt. It did end properly, but if Harris had written one last chapter or an epilogue, to show the after-effects of the events described or the future fate of the characters, it would have been better. A very personal opinion.<br /><br /><b>Rants:</b><br /><br />I believe the book's <b>greatest achievement</b> lies not in being a wonderful thriller, but in presenting the dark alternative had the course of the 2nd World War taken such a turn. What would have been our fates, if Germany led by Hitler would emerge as the biggest superpower of the world, and his crimes against the Jews gone unpunished? This horrifying thought is addressed very convincingly in the book. <br /><br />Indeed, the end that the SS was heading towards in the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/124914.The_Day_After_Tomorrow" title="The Day After Tomorrow by Allan Folsom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Day After Tomorrow</a>(Review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318818862" rel="nofollow noopener"> here</a>) is a reality here. People would have lost the power to think freely, and the freedom to question. The SS would keep tabs on you, and even your own 10 year son would be brainwashed to hand you over to the Kriminalpoleizi if you were suspected. Rape and incest would not be considered as sexual crimes, rather having conjugal relations with a person of Polish or otherwise 'unclean' origin, could result in a death sentence. <br /><br /><br />So, for all those who find the act of speculating 'What if?'s exciting, I would implore you to read this book. I'm sure it will prove to be a rewarding experience.<br /><br />3.5 shining stars. <br /><br />As for now, I guess I'll sit back and enjoy the <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gV5NV0LNtwY" rel="nofollow noopener"> TV show</a> based on the book, and see what they have made of it... </span>
  <a data-text-id="6928964761840674700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2542665040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2542665040" />
    <a title="Roopkumar Balachandran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45432931-roopkumar-balachandran"><img alt="Roopkumar Balachandran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569057781p2/45432931.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2542665040?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roopkumar Balachandran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roopkumar Balachandran" href="/user/show/45432931-roopkumar-balachandran">Roopkumar Balachandran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099571575" href="/book/show/13154433-fatherland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45432931-roopkumar-balachandran?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542665040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13951002217254084741">I have to thank Leah for her beautiful review of Fatherland which piqued my interest in alternate history. <br/><br/>The story is police procedural and based on the alternate history, if German had won the Second World War, the protagonist Herr Sturmbannfuhrer Xavier March, homicide investigator with the Berlin Kriminalpolizei, he previously worked in Kriegsmarine during WWII, married to Klara had a son named Pili, after promoted to Berlin his marriage failed. <br/><br/>On April 14th 1964 he was called to investiga</span>
  <span id="freeText13951002217254084741" style="display:none">I have to thank Leah for her beautiful review of Fatherland which piqued my interest in alternate history. <br /><br />The story is police procedural and based on the alternate history, if German had won the Second World War, the protagonist Herr Sturmbannfuhrer Xavier March, homicide investigator with the Berlin Kriminalpolizei, he previously worked in Kriegsmarine during WWII, married to Klara had a son named Pili, after promoted to Berlin his marriage failed. <br /><br />On April 14th 1964 he was called to investigate the death of an old man with a missing foot. Upon verification that old man was Buhler a senior civil servant who was close to Hitler. All of a sudden the case from him was withdrawn and given to Gestapo headed by Odilo Globocnik also known in SS as Globus. But March voluntarily starts to investigate with help of his friends. <br /><br />Then another case comes up now it is Doctor Wilhelm Stuckhart who was also a senior civil servant and close to Hitler. And another of their friend Martin Luther who becomes a fugitive, March understands that somehow these three are all involved. Witness mentions that Wilhelm Stuckhart killed himself before he had to give an interview to an American reporter Nightingale. The story takes a surprising twist when he comes to know more about Buhler, Stuckhart and Luther and their greediness. They have opened a bank account in Zurich, at first March assumed they might have put a hoard of money or art treasures without the knowledge of Reich but March on inspecting the account he finds documents and one old painting. <br /><br />Same time on the eve of Adolf Hitler 75th birthday March was kept under custody as he might reveal the secret to the world. What was that March found out through his painstaking investigation? <br /><br />A superb thriller from Robert Harris, all these days I was tagging along with March in the fictitious world of 1964. Like March we too will feel who to believe and who not to believe. The author has created a victorious Germany how their architectural brilliance will be if they have won the war, I remember a documentary of Hitler's Third Reich their ideas of Great Hall, the autobahns etc. A twist during the climax is predictable but a captivating, ingenious fast paced novel. <br /><br />Review with images click the link below.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.chromaring.com/2018/11/fatherland-book-review.html">http://www.chromaring.com/2018/11/fat...</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_3065825433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3065825433" />
    <a title="Kavita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5858699-kavita"><img alt="Kavita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315387023p2/5858699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3065825433?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kavita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kavita" href="/user/show/5858699-kavita">Kavita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=yawnfest">yawnfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=germany">germany</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3065825433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14139352250783348600">The premise of <i>Fatherland</i> is interesting. I have been waiting for years to read this book because of it. It is set in a world where the Nazis have won Second World War and are now a major power base in the world. This leads to a LOT of intriguing speculations about how the world might have turned out. Sadly, the book does not even come close to the potential this theme offers.<br/><br/>Harris has done his research, but it's a very basic and narrow research. He knows how the Nazi system functioned but noth</span>
  <span id="freeText14139352250783348600" style="display:none">The premise of <i>Fatherland</i> is interesting. I have been waiting for years to read this book because of it. It is set in a world where the Nazis have won Second World War and are now a major power base in the world. This leads to a LOT of intriguing speculations about how the world might have turned out. Sadly, the book does not even come close to the potential this theme offers.<br /><br />Harris has done his research, but it's a very basic and narrow research. He knows how the Nazi system functioned but nothing beyond that. Nothing of German cultural practices, nothing about how Germans live everyday. I mean, yes, we know they are oppressed but that's not really world-building. All the characters are cardboard-cut and don't offer much to a reader looking for a nuanced portrayal. Everything is Anglicised in this German world, you'd think they didn't really win the war! Even the hero is Anglicised, even his name. Why would you mess up a vital but easy thing like that?<br /><br />Harris also fails to give a real sense of how the world turns out. European countries are now a satellite to the German State, but what about other factors? The World War Two led to the end of colonisation - so what happens to the colonies? Do they get transferred to Germany, like what happened with Namibia, Togo, etc. after WW1? Or doesn't history change there? What about the Cold War? If the USSR never existed, or is supported by USA, where does Germany fit into the nexus? Harris misses great opportunities to really build a believable world that we can delve into. <br /><br />The great denouement is no surprise for anyone. But, for some reason, everyone in this world assumes that the extermination of the Jews twenty years ago is going to piss Americans off. I am not sure why they would do so without there being a really strong political reason. The US did send back Jewish refugees in 1939, so it's not a given. The plot fails here for me. It could have been done better without involving the US. It was just really sloppy plotting. <br /><br />And don't even get me started on that terrible American woman journalist character that seems to be taken from some stock character listing that authors are privy to. She seemed to exist only for two reasons: rah, rah, USA! and random sexist romance of middle aged man with a "beautiful" young woman. God forbid the random journalist woman is ever not described in terms of her looks. This mandatory romance is forced, useless, and boring. <br /><br />I am really annoyed at how bad this book is. It's like a Dan Brown book without the good parts! It's posture as an alternate history is an insult. Harris really doesn't bother much about anything but the stupid mystery, which is also not that interesting, and only focuses on the Nazi system, which admittedly he has researched well. But that's really about it. He seems to lack the acuity to write real alternate history, which would involve intense research about multiple subjects so that this type of linear narrative could be avoided and a better world built that encompasses world politics, German culture, etc.<br /><br />I am severely underwhelmed and I genuinely wonder if the high rating of this is only because of its theme of anti-Nazism and Holocaust denial. Because this really is a very badly executed book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14139352250783348600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10735760321722642998">8.5/10<br/><br/>This turned into a gripping read and by the end I was well and truly absorbed in this alternative reality and “what if” scenario of Germany winning the war. Although, I’ve read two books recently where Germany won the war. I’m starting to doubt my knowledge now…did the Axis powers really win?!<br/><br/>It took a while to get going in this book, presumably because a lot of information was provided in this alternative reality and making the reader aware of the police state and nervousness of any non-c</span>
  <span id="freeText10735760321722642998" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />This turned into a gripping read and by the end I was well and truly absorbed in this alternative reality and “what if” scenario of Germany winning the war. Although, I’ve read two books recently where Germany won the war. I’m starting to doubt my knowledge now…did the Axis powers really win?!<br /><br />It took a while to get going in this book, presumably because a lot of information was provided in this alternative reality and making the reader aware of the police state and nervousness of any non-conforming thoughts/opinions. But after the first sections got going this book picked up a head of steam. The whole murder mystery is done well with what seems like a standard death turning into a larger conspiracy theory which leads further down into a rabbit hole. <br /><br />Robert Harris is good at what he does and this is no different. He makes the story and setting accessible to everyone and it was a joy to read. The latter half of the book was spot on and if it wasn’t for a slower start I would have rounded this up to 5 stars. Harris is climbing up my list of favourite authors at a rate of knots.</span>

<div id="review_2699860476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2699860476" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2699860476?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18879231-fatherland">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2699860476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18178115900798209312">I first read this debut novel, by Robert Harris, when it was first released, in 1992, so it was interesting to go back and re-visit it over a quarter of a century later (has it really been so long?!). I recall that I read, “March Violets,” a few years earlier – Philip Kerr’s first Bernie Gunther novel was published in 1989, although there was a long gap between the original trilogy and Kerr’s taking up the character again. Robert Harris tends not to do series books so often, although he wrote hi</span>
  <span id="freeText18178115900798209312" style="display:none">I first read this debut novel, by Robert Harris, when it was first released, in 1992, so it was interesting to go back and re-visit it over a quarter of a century later (has it really been so long?!). I recall that I read, “March Violets,” a few years earlier – Philip Kerr’s first Bernie Gunther novel was published in 1989, although there was a long gap between the original trilogy and Kerr’s taking up the character again. Robert Harris tends not to do series books so often, although he wrote his Cicero trilogy, but you do wonder whether he considered a series for the main character of this novel, the world weary investigator, Xavier March.<br /><br />The premise of this novel is an interesting one. It is April 1975 and a week before celebrations for Adolph Hitler’s 75th birthday. Obviously, the Germans won WWII and the world is very different; although Harris thankfully still allows the Beatles to flourish and, indeed, to fulfil their musical obligations in Hamburg. Other than that, though, we are in a much darker world. The war finished in 1946, but rumbles on in the East, while March himself returned from service on a U-Boat to discover that the Jewish community where he lived had vanished. <br /><br />March is divorced; his ex-wife a good, Party member, and his ten year old son, Paul, ‘Pili’, happily denouncing him as not loyal enough. March, you feel, has been in some denial about how he is viewed. He even questions the whereabouts of a Jewish family, whose photograph he finds in his apartment. If he thought his uniform, and his job as a homicide investigator, were enough to keep him safe, he is very wrong.<br /><br />When the overweight body of a man is discovered, it seems to be just another crime. However, the body belonged to a high-ranking Nazi and, before soon, March is investigating what appears to be a conspiracy which goes straight to the doors of Reinhard Heydrich and in the origins of the Final Solution. March becomes involved with American journalist Charlotte, ‘Charlie,’ Maguire. Together, the two are determined to uncover the truth, but investigating in Hitler’s Germany is a very dangerous game. This is an interesting novel, with a lot to recommend it. It has the feel of a society which never climbed out of wartime, which, in many ways, Hitler’s Germany hadn’t in this book. A scary portrait of an alternative history, where most people unquestioningly accept the world mapped out for them.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18178115900798209312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K0GcPIYBJg9iMNbYvPN6jjPsipGsITEb56ioTeajiacyj/Cm5ldyOnSvtN8RARQXpGW13GxG60fdXZQVSIizww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9d5nk+PLAUY0W9mNDakJNx2V/XGAQ1tcUjc69XN2LnPsEAsJg51VcyLEu4qgW2euihzCPEAkgQBowgat3V0UFw==')})
  }

Then their mother loses her job due to political strife, and the family, facing poverty, becomes drawn into the New Church, an institution led by a charismatic pastor who is not shy about worshipping earthly wealth. \n\nSoon Bibike and Ariyike’s father wagers the family home on a “sure bet” that evaporates like smoke. As their parents’ marriage collapses in the aftermath of this gamble, the twin sisters and their two younger siblings, Andrew and Peter, are thrust into the reluctant care of their traditional Yoruba grandmother. Inseparable while they had their parents to care for them, the twins’ paths diverge once the household shatters. Each girl is left to locate, guard, and hone her own fragile source of power. \n\nWritten with astonishing intimacy and wry attention to the fickleness of fate, Tola Rotimi Abraham’s Black Sunday takes us into the chaotic heart of family life, tracing a line from the euphoria of kinship to the devastation of estrangement. In the process, it joyfully tells a tale of grace and connection in the midst of daily oppression and the constant incursions of an unremitting patriarchy. This is a novel about two young women slowly finding, over twenty years, in a place rife with hypocrisy but also endless life and love, their own distinct methods of resistance and paths to Tolkiens Hauptwerk, Der Herr der Ringe erzählt nur einen kleinen Ausschnitt, das Ende des dritten Zeitalters -- vorangegangen sind lange Jahre, deren Ereignisse den mythischen Untergrund von Tolkiens Welt bilden. Es handelt sich dabei um einen Ausschnitt eines wesentlich umfangreicheren Werkes, dem Silmarillion. Hier erzählt Tolkien von der Geburt der Welt in der Musik, von der Erschaffung der Elben und Menschen, der Zwerge und Orks, von den Ereignissen der drei Zeitalter und ihren leidvollen Schicksalen. Im Herrn der Ringe wird nicht nur häufig auf diese Ereignisse Bezug genommen, es leben auch noch einige der Protagonisten und ihre Nachfahren, und die Ereignisse des Ringkrieges sind nur eine Variation der alten Mythen. Das biblisch anmutende Silmarillion mag einige überfordern -- wer dennoch mehr über die Welt der Ringe und Elben erfahren will, für den ist Feanors Fluch eine reizvolle und andächtig stimmende <span id="freeTextContainer5030753585906238561">ROBERT HARRIS is the author of nine best-selling novels: Fatherland, Enigma, Archangel, Pompeii, Imperium, The Ghost Writer, Conspirata, The Fear Index, and An Officer and a Spy. Several of his books have been adapted to film, most recently The Ghost Writer, directed by Roman Polanski. His work has been translated into thirty-seven languages. He lives in the village of Kintbury, England, with his </span>
  <span id="freeText5030753585906238561" style="display:none">ROBERT HARRIS is the author of nine best-selling novels: Fatherland, Enigma, Archangel, Pompeii, Imperium, The Ghost Writer, Conspirata, The Fear Index, and An Officer and a Spy. Several of his books have been adapted to film, most recently The Ghost Writer, directed by Roman Polanski. His work has been translated into thirty-seven languages. He lives in the village of Kintbury, England, with his wife, Gill Hornby.</span>
